Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 103

— Hai Ke

Judge (to the criminal): You scoundrel, you have done so much evil, you are incorrigible. Have you ever been disciplined by your family in your life?

Criminal: When my old wife was alive, I was a good man. It's a pity she has been dead for a year. If the officials want me to abandon evil and return to righteousness, they must give me a wife. Otherwise, don't bother talking.

A: You and I have been friends for over ten years, and I dare not hide it from you. You are really too dull.

B: I don't think so myself. I don't know how dull I am. Why don't you tell me?

A: The clay bodhisattva in the City God Temple is more lively than you.

A: You went to the United States to investigate the economy this time. Have you seen their financial crisis there?

B: Yes, I did. One day, I personally experienced a financial crisis on the tram.

A: What happened?

B: When I was paying for my ticket, I accidentally dropped a gold coin under the seat. I searched all over the place, and others helped me search. After finding it, everyone thought it was theirs, and they started arguing. The police had to come to intervene. Isn't this a financial crisis?

A: Marriage is like sailing, the safety of the future is not guaranteed.

B: I'm not afraid of anything else, I'm most afraid of seasickness, so I dare not marry.

Snippets from a Press Conference and Social Gathering 104

— Huang Jiping

The Shanghai Journalists Association held its autumn social gathering on the 16th at the Tongxing Restaurant. The weather was fine and the sky was clear on that day. Members were all in high spirits and came together, some with their families. There were also guests attending, including some who had come from Kyoto from afar. In total, there were more than 130 people, a scale unprecedented in the past. I heard many anecdotes and would like to share one or two with readers.

Journalists should fulfill their duties

During the event, Committee Member Ge Gongzhen was elected as chairman. He reported on the association's affairs, first welcoming the guests and the assembled members. He then said that the association's publication, "The Journalist Weekly," had been published to its 27th issue, specializing in the status quo of the newspaper industry at home and abroad, which had been greatly loved by all sectors. He said that they were planning to improve the editing and increase the length of the article to spread it more widely. The association planned to raise funds to build a clubhouse to meet the needs of members' after-work entertainment. He also described the assistance given to Zhang Sixu and others this summer, as well as the death of Mr. Xie Jieshi, the founder of the association, and called on colleagues to stand in silence to mourn. The crowd then stood and silently mourned for two minutes. He continued by saying that in recent times, unification had been completed and the national fortune was on the rise. Freedom of speech had been declared, and the Fourth Plenary Session had resolved to convene a National Assembly on May 5th of next year. All colleagues should uphold the duty of journalists, serve the party and the country, and do their best for the people, so that the contribution of newspapers to the country and society would be even greater, in order to realize the ideal of a new China. Finally, he thanked more than 40 domestic goods factories for their generous gifts.

Resembling a temporary stage

Halfway through the dinner, the chairman invited members to perform, but some were reluctant while others volunteered. Then the guests, Mr. Wang Qingxun and Mr. Liu Yin, performed harmonica solos and duets. Mr. Wang said that the harmonica can play all kinds of music, each instrument costs only two or three yuan and can be learned in a few days. It is the wonder of family music. Compared to the violin, piano, brass music, etc., which cost hundreds of dollars and take two or three years to learn, it is like heaven and earth. He is planning to start the Chinese Harmonica Association to popularize it. Then, members Qian Ruifu, He Xiya, Feng Zhaoliang, Yu Kongwo, and Hang Shijun performed Peking Opera songs, with Yu Kongwo and Wang Ruoqi playing the piano. The singing of the old man, the old student, the female, and the blue shirt interspersed, bringing refreshing and pleasant emotions. After a song ended, the shouts of "Bravo...Bravo" and "One more" shook the house. The singers responded to the audience's request with one song after another, and only stopped after an hour. Other members wanted to continue the performance, but due to time constraints, they had to wait for another day. No wonder guests praised the talents of the press.

Fun facts from the event

A long table was placed in the restaurant, displaying gifts, including all kinds of clothing, food, and daily necessities. A gentleman laughed and said to me, "If this is moved to Nanjing Road to set up a tobacco and paper store, it would be enough to meet the needs of customers." Another gentleman said, "There are so many people here today. If a psychological test were conducted, the results would show that 60-70% of them came to divide the spoils." These are truly interesting words. The clothes and hats of the people attending the meeting were scattered all over a room, occupying more than enough space. The number of accumulated goods can be imagined. The restaurant was too large. When the chairman reported, the audience could not distinguish between each other, so he asked them to stand on the high platform and shout loudly. After speaking, he was exhausted and hoarse. There were quite a few female comrades who were good at singing, but most women were shy and did not perform. A certain lady suddenly left temporarily before singing, and only came back to receive the prize, which can be said to be good at advancing and retreating.

Everyone was happy after the banquet

After the banquet, gift vouchers were distributed. The vouchers were sealed in envelopes, each guest received one and each member received three. Those who received good prizes shouted with joy and were overjoyed. Those who did not receive a prize or received a consolation prize were disappointed. The consolation prize was inscribed with "I wish you good luck in the future," which was quite inspiring. The gifts were donated by more than 40 domestic goods factories, totaling more than 1,100 items, divided into 200 numbers. The preparatory committee members, Sun Daosheng and Hu Hanzhu, were responsible for the distribution and numbering in advance, which was very laborious and appreciated by all colleagues. The method of receiving the prize was to match the voucher number, and Sun and Hu, as well as Xu Chihen, Zhang Zhiren, and I, were responsible for awarding the prizes. The first prize was won by Mr. Li Zhusan, which was a set of crepe fabric from the Meiya Factory, worth 30 yuan. The items worth 20 yuan, 10 yuan, and 5 yuan were next in line, and the least was also worth 1 yuan. Some committee members initially showed humility and did not receive the prizes first, but in the end, they did not get anything, because there were also those who practiced "opportunism." In fact, although not all the guests came to receive the prizes, this move was enough to arouse common interest.

Record of a Strange Dog 106

— Wang Haizhu

Five days after the Beginning of Winter, the caretaker reported that Canglong had drowned in the water last night. Canglong was one of the dogs raised by the owner. The dog was blue-gray in color, hence the name Canglong (Blue Dragon). The death of a dog is nothing more than adding a pile of dirt, nothing strange. After a while, the servants all said it was a strange event, spreading the word with changed expressions. I hurried to the door and asked them to show me what they had seen. It was indeed strange. The owner woke up in the morning and did not know that the dog had died. He told his family that he had dreamed of his mother earnestly instructing him to maintain his personal conduct and teach his children as usual. Behind his mother stood a middle-aged maidservant with a thin face and dark clothes. His mother said, "This servant is loyal and diligent and still comes to guard our door. You should reward her." The family thought that it was because the funeral had just finished, and he was missing her. The owner thought to himself whether there was such a person among the servants of his ancestors. The gardener then reported the death of the dog. The owner said sadly, "That's it! This dog is female. Her clothes are dark and her face is thin, which matches the description. This is not a nightmare, but a strange dream." The family also sobbed and mourned. The owner ordered the servants to bury it in a deep pit in the shade of the garden. The owner also wrote a eulogy in the form of a couplet: "Traveling the road was difficult, a misstep became an eternal regret. Guarding the door was hard work, loyalty was higher than ordinary people." The words were earnest and the entrustment was profound. I also have the lines "Living, it barked at the immortal clouds, following Du Yu. Dying, it looked up at the Buddhist sun, reaching the lotus pond" to eulogize this strange dog. According to Tang Dynasty's Du Guangting, his family raised a dog named Feiyun. When the owner's grandmother, Du, returned to the Buddha, she once recited a Buddhist verse, and the curved pond where the dog drowned still had remnants of lotus pillows and blue waves. Therefore, I used it in a mixed way. More strange is that when Du's grandmother was about to die, three dogs barked for no reason, and this dog cried all night long. Therefore, dogs are also righteous and strange. I have written it all down for researchers of the soul to study.

What I Heard About Dumb Lovers Appearing on Stage 107

— Heng Zhuang

After the servant love case in Shanghai, the film company immediately made a film about the facts. At that time, someone also promoted that Huang Huiru would personally give a lecture on the beginning and end of the love affair. However, as a result, Huang Huiru not only failed to sacrifice her beauty, but also sacrificed her life first, so that the general public who longed for Huang Huiru never got to see the beauty of a celebrity. Not long after, the love affair between Wu Airong and the dumb Lin Jim occurred one after another. For a time, newspapers competed to report on it, and the momentum was no less than that of Huang Lu. Therefore, the current affairs film company also rose one after another and intensified its efforts, asking the person to star in the film "Dumb Lovers". Now that the film has been completed, it is scheduled to premiere on the 20th of this month at the Central Grand Theater, and I implore the two great lovers to perform funny dramas and lectures on the love affair. Lin Wu agreed, preparing to vent the grievances in their hearts and correct the misinterpretations of their love by society in the past.

Juan said that since domestic films have been taking social facts as the subject matter of the drama, and the owners of the facts have been the actors, and even the person has been asked to give a lecture on the course of events, this film should be the beginning of this.

Travel Notes from Nanyang (76) 108

— Ling Hua

The highest wage is three or four yuan per day. Those who are near the furnace and those who are on the top of the high level are easily infected with diseases by inhaling silver dust in the hot fire and soil ash into the lungs. I felt that my lungs were heavier after standing for a minute. How can I imagine doing this for years? However, if the injury is caused by the field system, the family will be compensated with hundreds of silver for injury to a limb and 3,000 yuan for death, but someone must apply for it, not everyone can get it. It is more worthy of investigation than the soldiers who died in battle. There are also workers who stand in deep muddy water to transport silver sand and mud, their faces are pale. Those who are near the furnace guard the red silver water and green firelight, watching the rotation of the machine's big wheels. Every time I think, is there really a hell of hot iron ruled by Yama in the world like this furnace, and beings are spinning in the Dharma wheel? Is it a delusion, or is it that everyone is using silver money fraudulently and has not seen the fire wheel in the silver field, so they do not know its manufacture and change? Then how can I determine that there is no bigger hammer than this field and that we have not seen it? I once entered a coal mine several miles in Taiyuan. Since then, I remember the suffering of coal workers every time I sit on the train. Now I have seen the silver field and sighed at the difficulty of using money. Who is spending money like dirt? Money is as lethal as cannonballs.

Among the strange customs of Nanyang, there are women of the White Ban Yi tribe who wrap their heads with cloth, which is unusually high, as much as one and a half feet. The cloth used is ordinary blue cloth. It is hot here, but they wrap their heads like this. However, there are also many women who do not wrap their heads or wear powder, their natural beauty is better than embellishments. There are two types of Ban Yi people here, one is the local Ban Yi, and the other does not speak the same language as Burmese. There is a Yunnan Ban Yi person who speaks the Dian language, just like a Chinese person, and is a mixed race.

Waking up on the morning of the 10th, the island sounds were pleasant and the green mountains reflected the people. The weather was about April and August, and single clothes were suitable. The weather in northern Burma is the best. China is too cold and the equator is too hot. The climate in northern Burma is the most suitable.

The great discovery of this trip to Nanyang that can be contributed to the world is that the great immigration business in Nanyang should be jointly operated by the international community in order to reduce class struggle and ease world wars. If the federation of Europe, Asia, and the Americas cannot be formed, then the Asian federation can be formed first. Nanyang can immigrate at least 100 million people. Why do the Japanese have to spend so much conspiracy in the eastern provinces to move so few people? A friend said that there are still places like Yeren Mountain outside the southwest border of Yunnan, which can accommodate tens of millions of people for thousands of miles.

Warmth in the Heart (317) 109

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 15: The Four Chambers Shed Tears, Sad and Red Feelings; The Seat Is Filled with Admiration, Lingering and Green Thoughts.

Long Ziyun was an old guest of the Bao family. He had known A Su since she was thirteen years old. He used to think she was gentle and pitiable, but now she was obviously slender and outstanding. In the past two years, several of the Bao family's Yun were accompanied by her to sing, so she felt that she had the material to respond. Her eyebrows could speak, and her every frown and smile seemed to have her own effect. Later, many guests called the Bao family's games for her sake. A Su's absence made people unhappy. Gradually, her position in the family became more powerful. Originally, in the Shanghai halls in the past, those who went out were called ladies, and those who accompanied them were called Sister A, with clear distinctions that could not be misrepresented. In name, there was a master-servant relationship. The talented people in the foreign circles also divided them into flowers and leaves, and they were often paired evenly. Often, the beautiful lady was not concerned with the one who accompanied her. It even went so far as to have an old woman accompany her. However, those who were fascinated would not hate this old woman, just like a famous artist who painted flowers, with a strange stone set off next to a beautiful flower, thus making it more beautiful. If the lady who went out was of mediocre appearance and of average talent, then the person who assisted her had to be a wonderful choice. This was like in the early monarchical political system, when the emperor was young, there had to be an experienced minister to assist him. Therefore, the young gentlemen in the halls also had to have a good Sister A to accompany them. To use flowers and leaves as a metaphor, although the flower is small, the leaves are very lush, and it is also moving. Moreover, there are those guests whose intention is not in the flower but in the leaves. In autumn, the red leaves are more beautiful than the flowers in February. If you think about it this way, you can see that the leaves can also be better than the flowers. Now, A Su can naturally be regarded as the famous leaf at that time. In less than half an hour, the games that were called came one after another. A Su came with Luyi as the third to arrive. When she arrived on the stage, she greeted her with a full greeting, calling Long Ziyun Fourth Master. Not only did she know everyone in the guest room, but she also knew most of the so-called little sisters in the game that were called. In the past, Sister A who followed the game used to fill the water pipes, but Long Ziyun did not smoke any kind of smoke. A Su smiled and said, "Fourth Master does not smoke water pipes, so we are considerate of us, and we are happy to save effort." She picked up a silver water pipe bag and stood next to her smilingly. She also said to the little girl Luyi, "Sister, Fourth Master knows you." She also said to Long Ziyun, "Fourth Master, please be tolerant. Our sister is coming out for the first time, and she is afraid that it will be difficult, and she is not willing to call anyone." Ling Zhixiang interjected from the side, "Okay, with you, Sister A Su, accompanying her, what are you afraid of?" At this time, Zuo Shichen, who was sitting opposite Long Ziyun, was staring at Luyi with both eyes, completely lost in thought.

French Concession Elects Chinese Directors and Committee Members 127

The Shanghai French Concession Taxpayer Chinese Association held a general election meeting yesterday (18th) at 3 PM in the Qilu Guild Hall on Ximen Road. Attendees included Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Shang Mujiang, Cheng Zhusun, Jin Liren, Zhang Jixian, Li Yingsheng, Li Weiliang, Yu Zicheng, Bei Zairong, Yan Qinxiang, Dong Kechang, Tao Leqin, Chen Dezhang, Dai Chunfeng, Zhu Yanzhi, Sheng Zhiren, and dozens of others. The Municipal Government's Social Bureau sent Ye Muju, and the Municipal Party Headquarters sent Mao Yuan, as representatives to attend and provide guidance.

After the bell rang and the meeting commenced, Shang Mujiang, Cheng Zhusun, and others were nominated as the presidium. They reported on the purpose of the meeting and then delivered opening remarks (recorded below). Next, the official correspondence between the French Consul General and the Association was read aloud. Then, ballots for the election of Chinese directors were distributed, and voting took place on the spot, with ballots placed into the ballot box. Jin Liren and Lou Hongjun were designated as ballot counters, and Tong Lizhang and Tao Leqin as ballot recorders. Upon opening the ballot box, thirty-two votes were found.

The results of the ballot count revealed that the candidates with the most votes, and therefore elected as Chinese directors, were: Zhang Xiaolin (31 votes), Du Yuesheng (30 votes), Zhu Yanzhi (28 votes), Wei Tingrong (28 votes), and Lu Bohong (26 votes). The next highest vote-getters were Huang Jinrong, Shang Mujiang, and Cheng Zhusun.

After the director elections were completed, refreshments were served, and then ballots were distributed and cast for the election of Chinese committee members. The results of this election were Shang Mujiang, Cheng Zhusun, Jin Liren, Zhang Jixian, and Li Yingsheng, among others, for a total of nine people.

The opening remarks and the correspondence between the French Consul General and the Association are recorded below.

(Opening Remarks)

Today, our Association holds a general election meeting to elect directors and committee members to the French Concession Board of Directors, who will serve as representatives of our Chinese taxpayers in executing and presiding over municipal affairs within the concession. This is something that deserves the utmost attention from our Chinese taxpayers. Our ultimate goal, of course, is to achieve freedom and equality for China, to complete the elements of an independent nation, and to recover the concessions, which is a common endeavor we should all undertake. However, in this transitional period, asserting the right to participate in municipal affairs and practicing such participation are necessary steps in implementing the principle of democracy, especially during the period of political tutelage, when we must strive to exercise the four powers. This is something that we all must strive to achieve. Furthermore, the future Board of Directors will be a board of directors for both Chinese and foreign residents, so all municipal facilities provided by the Board of Directors will be the responsibility of us Chinese taxpayers, because we will all be principals and there will be no room for excuses. This will prove that we have a deep understanding of both rights and obligations, and that we are not merely seeking the name of participating in municipal affairs without seeking the reality.

(Letter to the French Consul General)

Respectfully informing you that, regarding the matter of your esteemed Consul General entrusting our Association representatives to negotiate the political participation rights of Chinese citizens and the increase of representatives attending the Board of Directors, you agreed to promptly reply with the details of the agreement. However, we have yet to receive your esteemed reply. Therefore, we are writing again to request your reply.

Respectfully requesting Consul General Grieglynn.

French Concession Taxpayer Chinese Association.

(Reply from the French Consul General)

To the Esteemed Directors of the Shanghai French Concession Taxpayer Chinese Association:

Respectfully informing you that I have received your letter of the 16th of this month concerning the matter of Chinese citizen political participation and the addition of Chinese directors. This matter has been negotiated, and I am requesting a copy of the list of the five existing regular Chinese directors and the nine special committee members to facilitate verification.

Respectfully requesting your well-being.

Grieglynn, Chairman of the French Concession Board of Directors.

It is also reported that the inaugural meeting of the new and old Chinese directors and committee members is postponed to a later date due to the lateness of the hour.

Year-End Accounting Problem 128

The City Chamber of Commerce's Application for Modification Denied.

Social Affairs Bureau Orders Businesses to Hasten Preparations

The City Chamber of Commerce has reported that year-end closing of accounts presents difficulties for both agricultural and commercial situations. Various trade associations have repeatedly requested modifications, and the City Chamber of Commerce has specifically petitioned the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to request a change to the day before the Start of Spring as the closing date. The Bureau reportedly denied the request, stating that year-end closing of accounts according to the Gregorian calendar cannot be changed, and that Administrative Yuan Order No. 3850, instructing all provincial and municipal governments to follow this regulation, is on file and cannot be made an exception. Therefore, an order has been issued, the contents of which are recorded below.

Having read the petition, the Bureau finds that this year's Gregorian calendar year-end closing of accounts cannot be modified, as Administrative Yuan Order No. 3850 has already been issued to all provincial and municipal governments for compliance. The Chamber's request to use the day before the Start of Spring as the general closing date for businesses does not imply a desire to use the obsolete lunar calendar. However, business practices traditionally treat the year as a single accounting period, and bookkeeping records follow this example. This year, businesses have already followed the government's orders and recorded all information in their books according to the Gregorian calendar dates, with monthly summaries and annual closings conducted in accordance with the new calendar. Changing to February 4th would unnecessarily fragment the accounts and make calculations more difficult. This is the first reason.

Regarding the agricultural harvest season, according to the Twenty-Four Solar Terms issued by the central government, harvesting has already taken place around the Autumn Equinox in both the Yellow River and Yangtze River basins. The Frost's Descent term has passed, and preparations for winter farming have begun. By the time of the Start of Winter and Light Snow terms, farmers are idle and sell rice and beans for silver. This leaves more than a month to close the books before the year-end. There is no reason why accounting and settlement should be insufficient. The views of the Bean and Rice Trade Association, etc., seem somewhat limited to a corner, and the inland chamber of commerce seems to be indulging in old habits and resisting reform. The problem is clearly not purely about the accounting period. This is the second reason.

The Bureau notes that the three-term accounting system exists for the convenience of commercial and financial cycles, and there are also instances of month-end accounting. Logically, businesses have these various means of assistance, and the year-end closing is simply a general summary to assess the state of business profits and losses over the year, without affecting the length of the accounting period. Furthermore, the distance between accounting periods was previously five, three, and four months, but now it is five, four, and three months. Why is it necessary to seek an average? This is the third reason.

Regarding the various difficulties mentioned by the Chamber, if inland businesses had the same enthusiasm for complying with government orders as businesses in this city, there would be no difficulties. It should be understood that promoting the Gregorian calendar seeks uniformity in calendar administration, and that the consistent lunar calendar and accurate seasons are of great benefit to agriculture and commerce. This Bureau certainly knows that reform should not be rushed, but if it is deemed beneficial and related to government orders, compliance is mandatory. Otherwise, if everyone says they will wait until next year, procrastination and neglect will inevitably result. The late Premier Sun Yat-sen clearly established the correct calendar when the Republic was founded, but the promotion of the Gregorian calendar still requires our efforts today. The Chamber of Commerce should be a model for all businesses and should personally and actively urge members to prepare for the changes and not be mistaken. The request to use the day before the Start of Spring as the closing date cannot be approved. In addition to reporting the details of this order, this reply is issued for your information.

Mrs. Victor Bruce Flew to Korea Yesterday Morning 129

Safely Arrived in Seoul Today

British female aviator Mrs. Victor Bruce departed from Hongqiao Airfield at 7:30 AM yesterday, flying directly to Seoul, Korea. The journey is estimated to be approximately 500 miles, diagonally crossing the Yellow Sea, making it one of the most difficult legs of her journey since departing from England. Mrs. Bruce estimated that it would take approximately five and a half to six hours.

At approximately 7:20 AM yesterday morning, Mrs. Bruce received a report from the Xujiahui Observatory indicating that the weather was favorable, with a gentle breeze accompanying her en route. She then decided to depart. There were only about fifty people at the airfield to see her off. The heavy 青島 [Qingdao] aircraft slowly ascended and headed north. Mrs. Bruce will pass through Chongming and enter the Yellow Sea. Her only safety equipment for the sea is a rubber raft. However, nearby British warships along the route have been ordered to prepare to provide assistance if they receive a distress signal from the woman.

According to news from the Japanese Consulate, Mrs. Bruce's flight coincided with the period of major Japanese military exercises. Many important areas were under martial law and prohibited from flying. As a result, there were many twists and turns in the flight route. The previous day, Mrs. Bruce personally visited the Japanese Consulate to negotiate. Consul Iguchi met with her and presented the required route, requesting permission from the Japanese government to pass through. The Japanese Consulate sent an urgent telegram to the Japanese government, and at approximately 10:00 PM that evening, a reply was received from the Japanese government granting permission to enter Korea near 38 degrees North latitude, passing through Mokpo. After receiving the telegram, Mrs. Bruce departed from Shanghai yesterday morning.

According to a Jiji Press report from Seoul last night, British female aviator Mrs. Victor Bruce departed from Shanghai at 7:30 AM on the 18th, passed over Mokpo at 12:45 PM, and safely arrived in Seoul at 3:43 PM.

Twists and Turns in the Reopening of Silk Factories 136

Of the Shanghai silk factories that勉力 [did their best] reopened after heeding the advice of the Silk Industry Association, a total of thirty-two, twenty-three, including Xin Chang in Zhabei and Xin Zha, have already resumed normal operations. However, workers at nine silk factories, including Yuan Feng in Hongkou, are unwilling to accept wage cuts, leading to labor-management disputes. At the time, the trade union had a standing committee member (Eastern District Trade Union), Chen Zhongxiang, detained by the police precinct, who went to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to appeal. The trade union convened a workers' congress the day before yesterday, intensifying the labor unrest. The Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, the Civil Training Committee, the Public Security Bureau, and the Social Affairs Bureau jointly issued a notice ordering the factories to resume work immediately. The Silk Industry Association also notified the nine factories that they must resume work on the 19th (today). The nine silk factories, including Yuan Feng, immediately notified their employees to sign in and resume work. However, the staff members refused to sign, and even the female workers were hesitant. Therefore, the resumption of work at the nine silk factories on the 19th is likely to be difficult to achieve because the labor side has no sincerity in cooperating with the capital side. It is now reported that the government authorities have stepped in to mediate, and staff wages have been increased to 85%, while the female workers' wages, calculated at 85%, may not be a problem if it amounts to 50.1 cents.

Revision of Regulations on the Export of Prohibited Antique Books 137

Customs and Shipping Companies Strictly Enforce the Ban

The Ministry of Education, in order to preserve national treasures, requested a ban on the export of antique books. It was previously stipulated that editions printed in the Song, Yuan, and Ming dynasties, as well as palace editions printed in the Qing dynasty, and editions published more than ten years ago, etc., were prohibited. This matter was previously reported in this newspaper. It is now reported that the prohibition of these antique books has been difficult to enforce because a clear standard for selection and evaluation is needed for customs to follow. The Ministry of Finance has revised the prohibited book list, adding a list of prohibited items and the procedures for evaluation. The revised regulations have been sent to the Jianghai Customs and forwarded to shipping companies for compliance. The revised regulations on the export of prohibited antique books are recorded below:

(1) List of Prohibited Items:

A. Thread-bound woodblock-printed books and paintings printed before the first year of the Xianfeng reign in the Qing dynasty.

B. Original movable copper-type illustrated books. (Items A and B were added by the Ministry of Finance)

C. Yongle Encyclopedia

D. Official government archives (added by the Ministry of Finance)

E. Handwritten manuscripts and carefully proofread editions (this refers to original manuscripts written by the author, whether published or not, which should be prohibited). Carefully proofread editions, meaning editions proofread by famous people, should also be prohibited.

F. Surviving works by Sun Yat-sen that have not been printed.

(2) Evaluation Procedures:

A. For woodblock-printed antique books, the evaluation is based on the dynasty or year of printing. If the dynasty or year of printing is unclear, the date of the preface or colophon is used. If the date of the preface or colophon is unclear, the birth and death dates of the author of the preface or colophon are used.

B. If any doubts arise during the evaluation of the above items, the customs office must send the original book to the Ministry of Finance, which will consult the Ministry of Education for evaluation. If there are too many volumes, a few volumes may be randomly selected and sent to the Ministry of Education, or the Ministry may send a committee to evaluate them. For customs offices too far from Beijing, they may report to the Ministry of Finance, which will consult the Ministry of Education and instruct the local provincial or municipal education bureau to jointly evaluate the items with the customs office.

(3) Compliance by Shipping Companies:

Yesterday, when the shipping companies received this order from the Ministry, they instructed their export counters to pay close attention to declared cargo. If there are books to be exported, they must be inspected according to the Ministry's order before they can be loaded. The customs office is also paying special attention to inspecting export goods to check for the presence of antique books being illegally transported.

Shipping News 138

Japanese Heavily Purchasing Mahjong Tiles, Shipping Rates to Southeast Asia Rise

Shanghai shipping companies, including Butterfield & Swire, Jardine Matheson, Nissin Kisen, and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, have increased freight rates by 10% across the board due to heavy cargo volume to South China ports. The increase took effect yesterday. The freight rates for items such as cloth have also increased at the same time. For example, cotton yarn to Shantou has increased from 2.2 taels to 2.4 taels per piece, to Hong Kong from 2.5 taels to 2.8 taels, and to Guangzhou from 3.5 taels to 3.8 taels. Fabric to Shantou has increased from 7.26 taels to 8 taels per ton, to Hong Kong from 8 taels to 8.8 taels, and to Guangzhou from 12 taels to 13.2 taels.

Water Level in Haizhou Sharply Decreases

The water level in Haizhou has recently dropped sharply, making it impossible for larger ships to navigate. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has decided to temporarily suspend the 華輪 [Huā Lún] ship's service to Haizhou until the water level rises. Due to heavy cargo volume to Dalian, it has been decided to dispatch the 同華 [Tóng Huá] ship to operate on the Shanghai-Dalian route.

Demand for Mahjong Tiles Transported to Japan Increases

Chinese mahjong tiles were popular in the United States four or five years ago, but exports were banned due to inferior quality. Recently, mahjong games have become popular in Japan, and local production cannot meet the demand. As a result, many mahjong tiles are being purchased from China. In the past month, each ship to Japan has carried a large number of mahjong tiles, averaging about three tons per ship. This trend is continuing.

The Zhenru International Radio Communications Station, established by the Ministry of Communications, has successfully completed its trial transmissions. Direct telegraph service between China and the United States will be opened soon. The official opening ceremony is scheduled for December 1st. Representatives from the government, social organizations, and various sectors will be invited to participate.

Landlords Cannot Increase Water Prices First 140

According to a letter from Central Pharmacy, the Shanghai Concession Taxpayer Chinese Association reported that the pharmacy's premises are rented from the Catholic Church on Nanshan Road, Hongkou, and that the tenants are responsible for the water bill, which is collected by the landlord. Previously, the Association announced that water fees would be increased but were to be paid at the original price until the issue was resolved. When the church collected the October rent, the pharmacy paid the water bill at the original price, but the church's rent collector refused to accept it. Recently, the church sent another letter demanding that the increased water price be paid, or the water pipe would be removed and the lease terminated. The pharmacy specifically requested guidance from the Association. The Association replied immediately, stating, "Regarding your letter of November 15th concerning the water price increase, we have carefully read it. The investigation of the water price increase issue is nearing completion, and it will soon be decided whether to increase the price. The Catholic Church is only collecting the water fee on behalf of the water company, and your pharmacy is not refusing to pay the water fee, only temporarily not paying the 25% increase in accordance with public opinion. The Catholic Church's attitude is improper and may even involve tenancy issues. If the Catholic Church actually takes such action, it will cause public anger among all residents and lead to serious unfortunate events, for which the church will be responsible." A corresponding letter has been sent to the church for its information.

Appeal from the Changxing Coal Mine 142

The board of directors of the Changxing Coal Mine Company, whose mining rights were revoked by the Construction Committee, has been continuously striving for reinstatement without success. As the Fourth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang Central Executive Committee has opened, the board of directors has unanimously decided to continue to strive for reinstatement and convene a general meeting of shareholders to address the situation. The shareholders' representatives submitted a letter to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's secretariat for the Fourth Plenary Session, stating, "We, the Changxing Coal Mine Company of Zhejiang, which is entirely commercially operated, have been affected by the Qi-Lu wars since 1924, and have been seeking to resume operations. However, in the winter of 1927, the Construction Committee revoked the company's mining rights on the pretext, and sent personnel to the mine to forcibly operate it for three years. We have repeatedly appealed to various government agencies to report our unwarranted loss of employment. Recently, the Construction Committee used the name of the Changxing Coal Mine Bureau to publish notices in newspapers, forcing the company to send representatives to collect compensation bonds. We understand that we have put Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's Fourth Plenary Session proposals on file, stating that the government's recovery of privately owned mining businesses was a miscalculation, and proposed that privately owned industries should be encouraged and appropriately protected in the future. We are deeply grateful for Chairman Chiang and the committee members' concern for the people's hardships. The company has outstanding debts of over 3.1 million yuan to various banks in Shanghai over the years. After the publication of the compensation bond notices, the banking consortium and shareholders strongly opposed it and did not recognize the company's directors as having full responsibility to represent the shareholders. If they receive the bonds, the disputes with the shareholders and the banking consortium will never be resolved. We are fortunate that at the opening of the Fourth Plenary Session, Chairman Chiang and the committee members are upholding the protection of private property. We are taking the liberty of submitting this report and requesting that this case be submitted for public judgment. If we are given our mining rights back, it would be like a rebirth. We are urgently sending this telegram. We respectfully wish you well."

Pilot Training Institute Examines Pilots Yesterday 143

The Ministry of the Navy Sent Wu Zhennan as a Special Envoy

The Yangtze River Pilot Training Institute, established by the Ministry of the Navy within the Haidao Measuring Bureau at Fenglin Bridge, Xinzha District, is training pilots for the Yangtze River in preparation for the recovery of pilotage rights. Classes began in April of this year and have now reached the end of the academic year. The Ministry of the Navy sent Wu Zhennan, director of the Coastal Patrol Office, as a special envoy to conduct a thorough examination with the director of the institute, Yu Zhenxing, and the faculty. As most of the pilots are scattered at various ports along the Yangtze River, the examination period is set for three weeks. Yesterday was the first day of the examination. All pilots currently in Shanghai were ordered to attend the examination. A total of thirty-four pilots attended. The examination method consisted of written and oral tests. The pilots were able to answer the questions based on their coursework and experience. The results were excellent. This will lay a foundation for the country's future recovery of pilotage rights. The examination started at 2:00 PM and lasted until 5:00 PM.

Water Patrol Team Prevents the Shanghai Municipal Council from Building a Pier Across the Boundary 144

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession was previously building a pier near the Huzhang Shipping Bureau's pier on the Suzhou Creek, infringing on Chinese sovereignty. The Zhabei branch of the Pujiang Water Patrol Team intervened, and the work was stopped pending negotiations at a higher level. Recently, the engineering department of the Shanghai Municipal Council again sent workers to fill mud and drive piles at the old Garbage Bridge, preparing to build a pier. The Pujiang Water Patrol Team discovered this and sent Deputy Captain Dou to order the workers to stop working. However, the workers said that they were acting on orders from the engineering department of the Shanghai Municipal Council and refused to stop. Deputy Captain Dou told the foreman that the Suzhou Creek was entirely under Chinese sovereignty and that they could not work there without the permission of the Shanghai Municipal Government. If they dared to disobey, they would be arrested. The foreman then ordered the workers to stop working.

Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau Revises Three Sets of Regulations 145

I. Regulations for the Boat Tax Office

II. Detailed Rules for Collecting Boat Tax

III. Penalties for Boat Violations

The regulations of the Boat Tax Office of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, the detailed rules for collecting boat tax, and the penalties for boat violations have recently been revised by the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau and submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government for approval and promulgation. They are recorded below:

Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau Ship Tax Office Regulations 146

(Article 1) For the convenience of collecting ship tax in the urban area, the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, in accordance with Article 9 of the Bureau's Organizational Rules, has selected appropriate locations to establish ship tax offices to handle ship tax matters within the city area. (Article 2) The locations of the ship tax offices are as follows: (1) Jiadu (2) Suzhou Creek (3) Wusong (4) Chenjiadu (Article 3) Each ship tax office shall have the following officers: one chief clerk, one to two staff members, one to two collectors, one to two inspectors, and one secretary. The chief clerk shall be appointed by the director upon request to the Mayor. The remaining officers may be increased or decreased at the discretion of the director, depending on the workload of each office, and shall be appointed or hired by the director. (Article 4) The chief clerk of each ship tax office shall, under the command of the director and the supervising section chief, manage all affairs within the office. The staff members and collectors shall, under the direction and supervision of the chief clerk, be stationed at their respective posts and handle all collection, auditing, and clerical matters within the office. (Article 5) The donation slips for various ship taxes shall be separately specified. The collection procedures and working procedures shall be stipulated in detail in separate rules for compliance. (Article 6) To investigate and prevent evasion of ship tax, each ship tax office shall, with the approval of the director, establish inspection stations at important river and waterway passes for routine patrols. (Article 7) The collection hours of each ship tax office shall, in addition to the office hours stipulated by the Bureau, still assign staff to rotate on duty every dawn and on holidays to collect taxes. Night patrols shall also be dispatched to patrol strictly by boat to prevent evasion. (Article 8) Each ship tax office shall handle violations of Shanghai-bound ships in accordance with the relevant regulations for ship violations. (Article 9) After the daily collection deadline, each ship tax office shall, on the one hand, fill out a report with the number of donations, the number of vessels, the grade, the number of stamps, and the amount of fines, and send it to the second and third sections of the Bureau for verification. On the other hand, the collected donations shall be immediately deposited into the bank designated by the Bureau (those far from the route may apply for approval in advance). The remittance shall not be delayed. (Article 10) In addition to submitting a daily report every day, each ship tax office shall submit a weekly report at the end of each week and a monthly report at the end of each month for verification. The aforementioned weekly report shall not be submitted later than two days, and the monthly report shall not be submitted later than five days. (Article 11) The chief clerk of each office shall investigate and verify the use of stamps, donation certificates, and triplicate receipts by the collectors at any time to prevent corruption. All stubs and items that should be inspected shall be submitted to the Bureau for review together with the monthly report at the end of each month. (Article 12) Each ship tax office shall prepare the following main forms, registers, and vouchers: (1) Ship Tax Master Register (2) Income Book (3) Collection Report (4) Weekly Report (5) Monthly Report (6) Ship Tax Temporary Receipt (7) Quadruplicate Fine Receipt (8) Other various registers that should be needed (Article 13) All stamps, certificates, receipts, registers, and seals used by each ship tax office shall be printed and issued by the Bureau and shall not be manufactured or used without authorization. Similar receipts to silver money are strictly prohibited. Any violation will be investigated and dismissed. (Article 14) The chief clerk of each ship tax office shall evaluate the diligence or laziness of the audit personnel every month, list the merits and demerits separately, and submit them to the Bureau for rewards and punishments. Separate rules shall be formulated for the rules of rewards and punishments. (Article 15) In the event of resistance to donation by shipowners or other important matters, each ship tax office shall report to the Bureau for approval and may report to the nearest water and land police for assistance at any time. (Article 16) The collection personnel of each ship tax office shall be required to obtain a reliable guarantee from a well-established business firm in the city, which shall be sent by each ship tax office to the first section of the Bureau for personnel to investigate. In the event that the guaranteed store goes bankrupt or changes, they shall be ordered to find another reliable guarantee for everything. (Article 17) If there are any unfulfilled matters in these regulations, they may be amended at any time upon request. (Article 18) These regulations shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Fan Hesheng, Chairman of the Shanghai Rice and Grain Industry Association, submitted a document to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating that in order to protect the nation's vitality and maintain the farmers' economy, it is requested to prohibit the import of foreign rice, wheat, and flour. Our country was originally an agricultural country. In recent years, due to domestic military affairs and untimely droughts and floods, food shortages have been felt by the people, and they have been forced to purchase foreign rice as a temporary relief measure. The outflow of money has reached more than 100 million, and due to the relationship between expensive gold and cheap silver, the national economy is almost bankrupt. This year, the domestic rebellion has been quelled, the military affairs have been settled, and the autumn harvest is abundant. The people have plenty of food. The losses of farmers over the years and the nation's vitality are relying on recuperation and recovery. They are trying to transport large quantities of foreign rice, wheat, flour, etc. to China in order to destroy the economy of our farmers and the foundation of our country, which will be detrimental to the entire China. If this kind of poisonous policy of economic aggression is not strictly prevented, it will be more than enough to destroy China. It has been found that expensive rice hinders people's food, while cheap grain does not harm farmers. Therefore, the government bears the responsibility of concern for social livelihood and farmers' economy. It is specially requested to investigate and verify that in the Shanghai area, all groups related to people's food who have ordered goods from abroad should be required to register with your bureau by a deadline. Those who have not ordered goods should not continue to order. In the national aspect, it should be forwarded to the Municipal Government to request the National Government to issue an order to the coastal provincial governments and customs ports to prohibit the import of foreign rice, wheat, flour, etc. in order to protect the nation's vitality and maintain the farmers' economy. Pirates Clash 151

Fierce fighting twice on the sea off Juegang, nine out of ten houses on land are empty. A large number of pirate ships suddenly came to Fengli Juegang and other places outside Wusongkou. There were about 100 ships. According to the report from the 17th team of the 4th district of the Wusong Water Police, it was a feud between the pirate leader Pan Kaiwu and another pirate leader Shen Guanxi. Therefore, they gathered in the sea off the coast to discuss peace. At that time, the peace talks failed, and the two sides were about to fight. Gong Mianqin, the captain of the 17th team, dispatched a team of ships to quickly go to suppress the disturbance after receiving the report. It is now known that Pan and Shen, the two pirate leaders, gathered in the sea off the coast for many days, and the opinions of the two sides were extremely polarized, resulting in a breakup. Shen immediately led a large number of pirate ships to attack Pan's stock, sinking nine of Pan's pirate ships and drowning more than 100 pirates. Pan was defeated by his isolated forces and retreated to the sea off Lüsi. Pan was very uneasy after suffering this heavy blow, so he gathered more than 70 pirate ships under his command on the morning of the day before yesterday and sailed to the sea off Juegang to counterattack. Shen's bandits saw that the situation was not good and retreated north without fighting. Taking advantage of the victory, Pan's bandits occupied Shayugang, which had been occupied by Shen's bandits. The homes of the residents of the upper and middle classes on land had long been evacuated. When the two pirate ships fought, bullets flew everywhere, and they were all terrified. Therefore, most of them also moved to distant places. The area was almost nine out of ten empty, which is also said to be miserable.

Question of the Trial of the Zhao Assassination Murderer 152

County Magistrate Yan submitted a request to the provincial government for verification. Xia's confession provided a total of four accomplices in the murder. The Municipal Public Security Bureau will lift the arrest and confront the former criminal. The murderer of Zhao Tieqiao, Xia Shaoen, was interrogated repeatedly by Shen Jinghua, the director of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau. According to Xia's confession, there were a total of four accomplices in the murder of Zhao. One of them, Wang Xiaosanzi, was arrested and detained by the Municipal Public Security Bureau immediately after the assassination of Zhao. One was Xia Shaoen himself. There were still two people who had not been arrested. At this time, it was not announced. The four murderers were all instructed by someone before the assassination, and they received two-thirds of the reward in advance, tens of thousands of foreign dollars, which were collected by Wang Xiaosanzi and distributed equally to each person. They then carried two box guns, one pistol, and one six-round gun and waited in front of the China Merchants Bureau to prepare for the assassination. However, only Xia Shaoen among the four murderers knew Zhao Tieqiao, so it was decided that Xia would fire the gun. The other three protected him from the side. However, Xia Shaoen was not very familiar with the box gun he was carrying, and exchanged his pistol with Wang Xiaosanzi before shooting. He was hit. The Municipal Public Security Bureau learned that the confession of the previously arrested murderer Wang Xiaosanzi was generally the same as that of Xia Shaoen. However, there were still some discrepancies in several points, so they sent personnel to the County Public Security Bureau the day before yesterday to meet with Director Shen and requested that Xia be taken to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to confront Wang Xiaosanzi before being escorted back. Director Shen replied that this matter required a decision from the county magistrate. Therefore, he was not taken away at that time. County Magistrate Yan Shenyu resumed his duties after his leave the day before yesterday and read the confession of Xia Shaoen, the main murderer of Zhao, and the process of his arrest reported by Shen Jinghua, the director of the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, he submitted a report to the provincial government requesting instructions on the agency for hearing this case so that he could transfer it to the case for legal action. The provincial government will probably have instructions in the next few days.

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Regulations on Banning Dance Hall Girls 153

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau issued instructions to the district chiefs yesterday, stating: "Regarding the instructions, the dance halls in this city that have been approved and licensed by this bureau have many locations. However, the number of dance hall girls who operate by dancing in each dance hall is still unknown, and it is also impossible to distinguish between these dance hall girls and non-commercial dance hall girls who dance in the same hall. It is not enough to organize and facilitate inspections without registering them. Now, this bureau has formulated thirteen regulations on the registration of commercial dance hall girls in Shanghai and attached the forms of application, registration certificates, and badges, which have been submitted to the municipal government for approval. The instructions stated that the regulations and application forms drafted by the submission and attachments have been revised by this government, and the style of the registration certificate and the style of the badge are still usable. In addition to the regulations being promulgated separately, we have copied the articles and application forms and sent them to the bureau, so that they can be followed and implemented. This order and the original attachments are stored, etc. Therefore, the necessary application forms and badges, etc., have now been prepared separately and will be registered from November 25. In addition to the announcement and distribution, the regulations have been copied and sent to the districts for uniform compliance. This order.

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Regulations on the Registration of Dance Hall Girls for Business (Article 1) All women who operate by dancing in the urban area of this city must uniformly apply to this bureau for registration. (Article 2) To apply for registration, you must first obtain an application form and fill in two copies of the following items, together with two recent half-length photos, and submit them to this bureau for review: (1) Name (2) Age (3) Place of Origin and Current Address (4) Which School Graduated From (5) Where Studied Dancing (6) Family Status, and the Name and Occupation of the Husband if Married (7) Currently Operating in Which Dance Hall and the Name of the Hall Owner (Article 3) After registration is approved, a registration certificate and a badge will be issued. The dance hall where the person is located will prepare a registration fee of two yuan and the stamp will be collected on behalf of the applicant. (Article 4) When operating, the badge should be hung on the left of the collar. (Article 5) Women under the age of sixteen are not allowed to operate as dance hall girls. (Article 6) The business hours must comply with the provisions of Article 6 of the Shanghai Dance Hall Business Regulations. (Article 7) When changing professions, the registration certificate should be submitted to the dance hall where the person is located and submitted to this bureau for cancellation. (Article 8) If a dance hall girl is operating in Dance Hall A and also operating in Dance Hall B, or changes to operate in another dance hall, the hall owner should report to the competent district in writing at any time and report it to this bureau. (Article 9) If a dance hall girl engages in improper behavior during business hours, she will be investigated and dealt with according to the facts of the crime and according to the law. (Article 10) Violations of the provisions of Article 1 and Article 5 of these regulations will be fined up to 15 yuan and their business will be suspended. (Article 11) Violations of the provisions of Article 7 of these regulations will be fined up to 10 yuan. (Article 12) Violations of the provisions of Article 4 and Article 9 of these regulations will be fined up to 5 yuan. (Article 13) These regulations will be implemented from the date of submission to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgation.

Tan Meiying's Request for Divorce Original Status 154

Zhao Tan Meiying of Suzhou recently requested a divorce from her husband Zhao Guangzu. It was reported in a previous newspaper, but the previous newspaper did not provide detailed information. Now, we are recording the original status below. Plaintiff Tan Meiying, 22 years old, No. 8 Chunhui Lane, West Gate, Shanghai, Wuxian. Defendant Zhao Guangzu, 23 years old, No. 60 Jingxin Lane, Huade Road, Tilongqiao, Baoshan, is to state that the defendant is unable to live together and request a divorce. Statement of matters subject to judgment: (1) Request the court to order that the marriage between the defendant and the plaintiff be approved for divorce. (2) Order the defendant to bear the litigation costs. Statement of the lawsuit: The plaintiff was betrothed to the defendant by a matchmaker in childhood. Later, because the defendant was a young dandy, he easily went astray. Relatives strongly advocated marrying the plaintiff early in the hope of persuading him from the side. They were married on the 18th day of the first month of this year. However, after the plaintiff passed through the door, the defendant still indulged in prostitution and revelry, and became entangled with Concubine Mei Lao Jiu, making an engagement to marry her. In his eyes, he regarded the plaintiff as a thorn in his side. He lingered day and night, forgetting to return home and squandering his family property to the point of almost bankrupting his property. The plaintiff could not bear to see the inheritance of his grandfather and father, which came from sweat and blood, being squandered by the defendant at once. They quarreled morning and night, but unexpectedly, it aroused his anger, causing the plaintiff to be beaten repeatedly, which was witnessed by the maids. He even threatened her with a self-defense pistol, which was often dangerous. Because he loved Concubine Mei, he even wrote two letters to demand a divorce, forcing the plaintiff to end the marriage relationship. The plaintiff, burdened by the old etiquette, temporarily tolerated him to see what would happen later. Who knew that the defendant would take an inch and treat her even worse. The plaintiff, in order to cut off the fuel under the cauldron, filed a criminal lawsuit against Concubine Mei in your court in the hope that the defendant would realize his mistakes as soon as possible, but it was not too late. He was sentenced to a prison term in the case. Unexpectedly, the defendant held a grudge because of this and searched for trouble day and night without interruption. Recently, he left without saying goodbye and has been away from home for many days. It is obvious that he deliberately abandoned her and sent threatening letters, falsely claiming that he was kidnapped and demanding money. Such behavior is like a rogue. He cannot maintain a peaceful family and restore the joy of life. If he continues to abandon her like this, not only will her livelihood be affected, but also because the defendant is driven by lust, she is afraid that there will be unexpected dangers. What's more, the defendant has repeatedly expressed his intention to divorce, which shows that he has broken off relations. He has no choice but to request the dissolution of the marital relationship to extend his life. In addition to the return of the dowry, clothes, and the payment of compensation, which should be requested in another petition, he is hereby filing a petition requesting your court to order the defendant to appear in court for trial and judgment in accordance with the law. It is said that the court has approved the petition and ordered the summons.

Shanghai Commerce Gradually Recovers Its Former Appearance 155

The Shanghai Evening Post said that Shanghai's commerce can gradually return to its usual state. The total value of imports and exports in October increased by more than 10% compared with the first nine months of this year. The value of exports reached 39 million taels, and the value of imports reached 44 million taels, which is also an increase compared with the same month last year. According to import and export merchants, the sudden boom in trade this month is largely due to the end of the war. At present, domestic finance is gradually circulating and business is gradually booming. Even in Shanghai, local trade is more prosperous than before, especially the demand for building materials and machinery. According to Gabang, the Canadian Commercial Commissioner in Shanghai, the amount of lumber shipped to Shanghai has doubled compared with previous years. Although this is largely due to the loss of lumber sales in other countries, it may not be possible to indicate the good market conditions for building materials. In addition, the amount of food shipped in has also increased significantly. For example, the amount of canned food imported in October was more than in any other month this year.

Theatrical Bandits in Taixing Arrested in Shanghai 157

Liu Jicheng Allowed to be Taken Away for Investigation　　Detectives Reprimanded for Unauthorized Arrest. The Judicial Police of Taixing County Government, Weng Yuan and Chen Lang, along with informant Wang Peichun, came to Shanghai to investigate and arrest the wanted criminal Liu Jicheng, a native of Taixing. The previous day, they learned that Liu was living at 752 Yulin Lane, Yangshupu. Chen immediately ordered Weng and Wang to go to the address to apprehend Liu, while he reported to the local police station for assistance. When Weng and Wang arrived at Liu's residence, they found him packing his belongings as if preparing to leave. They immediately detained Liu and handcuffed him. Soon after, Chen arrived with Chinese and foreign detectives, took Liu to the police station, and detained him until the following morning, when he was escorted to the Special District Local Court. Judge Ge conducted the trial. The police station's lawyer stated that Taixing County claimed the defendant was a communist, but the police station's search of his house yielded no communist evidence. Therefore, if the county wanted to extradite him, they should first provide proof. As Weng and Wang did not report to the police station before making the unauthorized arrest, the police station is now prosecuting them under Articles 165 and 316 of the Criminal Law and requested a trial. The Chinese and foreign detectives presented the handcuffs as evidence. Chen Lang presented the official documents from the county government, requesting permission to extradite Liu and stating that Liu Jicheng, originally named Wang Kaiyuan, was indeed a communist and had committed serious crimes of murder and arson in his hometown. Informant Wang Peichun could testify to this. Wang Peichun then testified that he knew the defendant. On July 17th of this year, bandits suddenly came to our village, numbering two or three hundred. Villagers were robbed door-to-door, and before leaving, they committed murder and arson. The bandit gang was led by the defendant. His accomplice, surnamed Wang, has already been apprehended in Taixing. Judge Ge questioned the defendant Liu Jicheng. Liu stated that he had been living in Yulin Lane in Shanghai for about two months. Before that, he was a primary school teacher in his hometown. Last year, our village was attacked by bandits, and my house was burned down. Therefore, I left my hometown to seek refuge, first in Suzhou and then in Shanghai, and so on. Judge Ge, after reviewing the testimonies, ordered that Liu Jicheng be handed over to Chen Lang, the legal police of Taixing County Government, to be taken back for trial. Subsequently, the case of Weng and Wang being accused of illegal arrest was heard. Weng and others claimed that they were new to Shanghai and did not know the regulations of the concession. Moreover, the suspect was attempting to escape at the time, so they acted in haste and requested leniency. Judge Ge, considering that the two had made procedural errors and were new to the area, reprimanded them in court and ordered that the relevant officials be notified for legal action. Chen and others, upon hearing the verdict, immediately left.

He also thought about the frequent civil unrest in the country and worried that he would have no burial place after his death. The more he thought about it, the more frightened he became. Since then, he remained silent and expressionless. Yesterday (the day before yesterday), due to mental disorder and troubled thoughts, he went out to buy a bottle of black medicine and swallowed it. Soon after, his stomach felt extremely hot and painful. He unintentionally ran to the Jiangxi Road Bridge and jumped into the river to commit suicide. He was completely unaware of what happened after being rescued and taken to the police station. The mooring ropes of Mao's boat could not hold, and they suddenly broke. The hull drifted away. Ah Mao, a crew member (19 years old), was unable to do anything. His body is missing. Yang Xiaozheng, the cook of the boat, returned to the boat from the shore and saw that the incident had occurred. He immediately reported it to the brokerage, which in turn reported it to the Water Police Station to find ways to salvage the body of the deceased and the scattered tung oil. Robbery with Injury in Pengpu Town at Night 165

The Xu Family, a Wealthy Household, Lost Thousands of Dollars. The Next Day, Searching for Lost Items, Six People Detained. Xu Yisun, Xu Yousun, and Xu Dongsun, farmers from Zhangjiazhai, north of Pengpu Town in Baoshan, have been engaged in farming for generations. They are diligent and thrifty, and can be called the richest family in Pengpu. They live together in a two-courtyard deep residence with around 300 or 400 acres of farmland. During the Lu-Qi War, they were once looted by defeated soldiers, suffering significant losses. Unexpectedly, on the 16th night around 12 AM, dozens of bandits suddenly came, mostly speaking with a Jiangbei accent. They were wearing short clothes and carrying sharp knives and iron bars. They used a large stone to break down the gate and rushed in. By the time the whole family heard the noise and woke up, the bandits had closed in. Four bandits guarded outside, yelling with weapons, while the rest entered and ransacked the house. All seven rooms were emptied. Even the earrings, gold hairpins, and gold rings on the women's heads were taken. The loss of clothes, ornaments, and money was no less than several thousand dollars. Dongsun's son and his wife tried to escape to report to the police, but they were beaten on the head and face with sharp knives and iron bars, causing blood to flow freely. His son took the opportunity to escape through the back door, crossed the pool river, and blew the police whistle and shouted to catch the robbers. The bandits then howled and fled. By the time the nearby security team arrived with guns to arrest them, the bandits had already escaped far away. The next day at noon, three young men with disheveled clothes and strange behavior wandered around their house and lingered in the grass around the house, seemingly looking for lost items. Yisun and others, seeing this, became suspicious and followed them to Pengpu Town and reported them to the police. All six were detained. Yisun and others believed that there must be a reason for them to wander around the grass, so they went to check and found a flashlight in the grass. This item must have been lost by the bandits and they came to find it. They also reported it to the Pengpu Public Security Bureau substation for investigation.

Enemies Become Relatives 171

A Good Marriage Achieved. Guo Rugen, an 18-year-old from Chaozhou, has been working as an apprentice in a dyeing and weaving factory on McGon Road. Last year, through the introduction of a friend, he met a Wang girl, Ruifang. Wang, 28 years old, is beautiful and originally from Dinghai. She often came to Shanghai with her mother to visit relatives living at a certain address in Xianyi Lane on Xin Chongqing Road. Guo, taking advantage of his proximity, often visited her during his spare time, or went out with her. Therefore, cinemas and game venues in Shanghai often had their footprints. Since they met, the two have been very affectionate and close. Initially, they were able to maintain a friendly relationship. However, on a certain night in mid-June, Guo invited the girl to meet at the Beijing Grand Theatre. They whispered sweet words and were extremely happy. After the movie ended, they stayed overnight at the Central Hotel. The girl was bound by love and could not refuse. That night, she lost her virginity. Three days later, after the girl returned to her relative's house, she was severely questioned by her mother. The girl was ashamed and almost committed suicide. Later, through the persuasion of relatives and friends, she realized that what was done could not be undone and should not be publicized. Therefore, she sent someone to the Guo family to get things done, so that the event can be consummated. However, Guo's parents firmly opposed it. Their son was willing to keep his promise to wait until he could support himself and had enough money to marry her. The girl's mother, in order to make things happen, agreed to lend several hundred dollars for the wedding expenses. However, Guo's parents were still stubborn and refused. Therefore, the woman was furious and hired lawyer Tian Heming last week to send a letter of warning to Guo's parents, instructing them to indicate the definite date of the marriage within this week, otherwise, she would file a criminal lawsuit in court. Guo's family was terrified after receiving the letter and quickly sent someone to Wang's house to beg for peace. It is now known that the two sides have reached an agreement. The Guo family will marry the Wang girl within the month. A lawsuit has disappeared without a trace. From then on, enemies became relatives.

Publication of "What Pregnant Women Need to Know" 174

According to the estimates of public health experts, no fewer than 210,000 pregnant women in our country die each year due to childbirth, and at least 150,000 of them die from improper surgery and medication, which is shocking. Dr. Zhu Changya, a medical doctor, based on her love of guarding children and her experience and insights from studying obstetrics in hospitals at home and abroad for more than ten years, has written a book called "What Pregnant Women Need to Know." Matters that pregnant mothers and fathers should pay attention to, evidence of pregnancy and childbirth, hygiene during pregnancy and after childbirth, preparations for childbirth, etc., are all reviewed. Each book is priced at two corners, and it is sold in all branches of the Commercial Press.
